Hadd and Rasm
intermediate
8 min
Division Does Not Yield Definitions
Refutation of division for definition acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why logical division (qisma) cannot produce a definition and identify the two main objections from the passage.

Core Idea
Division presents options; picking one is an act of choice, not logical derivation.

Some logicians thought that dividing a genus into species and then selecting the correct species could yield a definition. The author refutes this: division alone gives indefinite branches; to select one branch requires external knowledge. Even if one uses exclusive disjunction (e.g., man is either rational or non-rational animal), the premises of that disjunction need proof, and division alone is insufficient.

Guided Path
1
Understand the proposed method
The method claims: divide the genus into its species, then exclude all but one species to arrive at the definition. Example: 'Man is either rational animal or non-rational animal; the second is not a definition, so the definition is the first.'
2
First objection: division implies indefinite branches
The division does not determine which branch is the definition; any specific selection is a 'positing' (waḍʿ) that is beneficial but not derived from the division itself. Find the phrase 'وضعا مفيدا لا مستفادا من القسمة'.
3
Second objection: exclusive division requires proof
Even if you use a disjunctive syllogism (e.g., 'Either A or B; not B; therefore A'), you must prove that the disjunction is exhaustive and that the excluded premise is false. These proofs are not supplied by division.
4
Additional objection: definition of definition issue
The author also notes that the method assumes a definition of 'definition' (al-qawl al-mufaṣṣal), which itself requires proof. This leads to a circularity or infinite regress.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if it is predicated absolutely, it does not necessarily follow that it is a definition of it, even if its predication of it follows, because of the possibility that its predication of it is by another way other than the predication of the definition of the defined. And just as its acquisition cannot be by what has passed, so too it cannot be from the definition of the opposite, as that its definition is the opposite of its opposite; for the definition of the opposite is not free from being acquired from its opposite, in which case circularity follows, or from other than its opposite; and that is subject to denial unless that other is the definition of this thing. Moreover, the definition of one opposite is not more known than the definition of the other opposite; so how can it be acquired? And because it is not necessary that every defined has an opposite. There has already passed what is not receptive of an opposite, like evenness and oddness, straightness and curvature, and others. And even if it were so, it would not be possible from the definition of the opposite. For if it were possible, either it would be in need of it in general; in which case it would follow that what is undefined is defined; or it would not be in need of it at all, in which case it would follow that it is not in need of it when it cannot be from other than it, and that is impossible. Rather, the way in acquiring the defined and its divisions is composition. That is by taking a number of individuals that are not divisible from the totality of the defined, whether the defined is a genus or a species; and seeking all their predicates up to the universal term above which there is no more universal. And those predicates may be essential, and may be accidental: so the essential are distinguished from the accidental by the rules that have been mentioned. Then the most universal essential that has nothing more universal above it is found. Then what is below it among the essentials likewise in order until it ends.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of four alleged methods for acquiring definitions (ḥadd), followed by the proposal of the correct method, which is composition (tarkīb). The author first argues against acquiring definition through syllogism. The syllogism fails because the major term would need to be a definition of the minor, but the syllogism only predicates the major of the minor without guaranteeing that predication is definitional. Moreover, the middle term applies to the minor's differentiae and properties, making the major not a definition of them. The second refutation targets division (qisma). Division yields indefinite branches; to obtain a definition, one must arbitrarily select a branch, which is not derived from division itself. Even if one uses exclusive division (e.g., man is either rational or non-rational animal), this presumes the truth of the conditional premise and the exhaustive nature of the division, both of which require proof. Thus division alone does not produce the definition. The third refutation concerns induction (istiqrā'). Induction cannot yield a definition because individuals as such have no definitions (they are corruptible). Even if we concede definitions for individuals, the definition of individuals does not extend to the species (each individual has unique accidents). Predicating a definition across individuals absolutely does not guarantee it is a definition of the species. The fourth refutation addresses acquiring definition from the opposite (ḍidd). This leads to circularity (if the definition of one opposite depends on the other) or requires an external definition, which is essentially conceding the point. Moreover, not all things have opposites (e.g., evenness, straightness). Thus these four methods are invalid. The correct method is composition (tarkīb): one takes several indivisible individuals of the genus or species, collects all their predicates up to the most universal, separates essential (dhātiyyāt) from accidental (ʿaraḍiyyāt) using established rules, and then arranges the essential predicates from the most universal downward until the definition is reached. The text cuts off mid-explanation.

Key Terms
قسمة
حد
مقدمة استثنائية
مصادرة

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does division alone not yield a definition?
A) Because division always produces an infinite number of branches.
B) Because selecting one branch requires external justification, and the conditional premise used in exclusive division needs proof.
C) Because division is only used for accidental properties, not essences.
D) Because division requires a definition of definition, which itself cannot be produced.

Key Takeaway
Division presents options but cannot determine which option is the correct definition without additional knowledge.

Induction Cannot Define
Refutation of induction for definition acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three reasons why induction (istiqrāʾ) fails to produce a definition, as given in the passage.

Core Idea
Individuals are corruptible and have no definitions; even if they did, the species would still elude induction.

Induction gathers data from particulars to form a universal. For definitions, one might think that by examining many individuals, one can extract the common essence. The author refutes this with multiple objections: individuals as such have no definitions (they are corruptible), the definition of individuals does not apply to the species (each individual has unique accidents), and even if you predicate something of all individuals, it does not guarantee it is a definition—it might be an accidental predication.

Guided Path
1
First objection: individuals have no definitions
The author asserts that individuals (ashkhāṣ) as individuals are corruptible (fāsidāt) and thus do not have definitions in the strict sense. Definitions apply to eternal species, not transient individuals.
2
Second objection: definition of individuals does not define the species
Even if we concede definitions for individuals, each individual has properties not shared by the species (e.g., unique accidents). Therefore, a definition that fits all individuals would include only what is common to all, but that common part may not be the whole essence of the species.
3
Third objection: predication of a term does not imply it is a definition
If you predicate a term of all individuals, it might be predicated in a non-definitional way (e.g., an accidental property). Hence, induction does not guarantee that the predicate is the definition of the species.

Source Text

بالماهية. ولأن الكبرى كاذبة حينئذ فإن الأوسط كما حصل للأصغر حصل أيضًا لفصوله وخواصه؛ ولا يمكن أن يكون الأكبر حدا لشيء منها. وأما الثالث فلأن القياس حينئذ لا ينتج إلا حمل الأكبر على الأصغر بالوجه الذي مر ذكره؛ وإنه من جملة ما لا حاجة له إلى البيان. ولأن المطلوب في هذا المقام هو أن يكون الأكبر حدا للأصغر؛ وذلك لا يلزم من القياس. وأما أنه لا يمكن أن يكون اكتسابه بالقسمة فلأن القسمة مستلزمة لأقسام غير معينة، فإن وضع قسم منها على التعيين ليكون حدا كان ذلك وضعا مفيدًا لا مستفادًا من القسمة. وإن استثني نقيض بعض الأقسام لإنتاج الباقي كما يقال حد الإنسان إما حيوان ناطق وإما حيوان غير ناطق ؛ والثاني ليس بحد فالحد هو الأول. أو يقال الإنسان إما حيوان وإما غير حيوان لكنه لا يكون غير حيوان فهو إذن حيوان؛ وبهذا الطريق يثبت أنه ناطق أو مائت. ثم يجمع جميع هذه المحمولات المساوية له ويقال أيضًا إنها قول مفصل دال على ماهية الإنسان. وكل قول مفصل دال على ماهية الشيء فهو حده فيقال لا يسلم أن القسمة منحصرة فيما ذكرتم من الأقسام؛ ولا يسلم أن المقدمة الاستثنائية صادقة لا بد من إقامة الدليل على كل واحد منهما. وبتقدير التسليم لا تكون القسمة وحدها مفيدة للحد. ولأنه بيان للشيء بما هو أخفى منه فإن حد الشيء وأجزاؤه أبين بالنسبة إليه من الغير. ولأن القول المفصل الذي مر ذكره حد الحد فتوسطه في القياس يكون مصادرة التوسط فإن معنى الشيء لا يكون بينا لشيء إلا وأن يكون بينا له؛ إذ ليس هو شيء غير معناه فعلم أن توسط حد الأكبر لأنه أبين للأصغر، أو حد الأصغر لأن الأكبر أبين له لا يفيد المطلوب. وأما أنه لا يمكن أن يكون اكتسابه بالاستقراء فلأن الحد إذا حمل على الجزئيات بعد استقرائها على أنه حد لكل منها من حيث هو معين فباطل لما بينا أن الأشخاص من حيث هي أشخاص لا حدود لها لكونها من الفاسدات وإن سلمنا ذلك لكن حد الأشخاص الواقعة تحت النوع لا يكون حدا للنوع؛ فإن لكل واحد من الأشخاص ما ليس للنوع. وإذا حمل عليها على أنه حد نوعها فهو مصادرة على المطلوب. وإذا حمل عليها مطلقا فلا يلزم منه أن يكون حدا له وإن لزم منه حمله عليه لاحتمال أن يكون حمله عليه بطريق آخر غير حمل الحد على المحدود. وكما أنه لا يمكن اكتسابه بما مر فكذلك لا يمكن من حد الضد كما أن حده ضد ضد ضده ؛ فإن حد الضد لا يخلو من أن يكتسب من ضده وحينئذ يلزم الدور، أو من غير ضده؛ وذلك في حيز المنع إلا وأن يكون ذلك الغير هو حد هذا الشيء . ثم حد أحد الضدين ليس أعرف من حد الضد الآخر؛ فكيف يمكن اكتسابه ولأنه لا يلزم أن يكون لكل محددة ضد. وقد مر من قبل ما لا يكون قابلا للضد به كالزوجية والفردية والاستقامة والانحناء وغير ذلك. ولو كان كذلك فلا يمكن من حد الضد. فإنه إذا أمكن فإما أن يفتقر إليه في الجملة؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون محدود ما ليس بمحدود، أو لا يفتقر إليه أصلا وحينئذ يلزم أن لا يكون مفتقرًا إليه إذا لم يمكن من غيره، وإنه محال بل الطريق في اكتساب المحدود وأقسامها هو التركيب. وذلك بأن يؤخذ عدة من الأشخاص التي لا تنقسم من جملة المحدود جنسا كان المحدود أو نوعا؛ ويطلب جميع محمولاتها إلى الأمر العام الذي لا أعم فوقه. وتلك المحمولات قد تكون من الذاتيات، وقد تكون من العرضيات: فتقرر الذاتيات من العرضيات بالقوانين التي مر ذكرها . ثم يوجد الذاتي الأعم الذي لا أعم فوقه. ثم الذي دونه من الذاتيات كذلك على الترتيب إلى أن ينتهي
with the quiddity. And because the major premise is then false, for the middle term as it is obtained for the minor is also obtained for its differentiae and properties; and it is impossible for the major to be a definition of any of them. As for the third, because the syllogism then only yields the predication of the major of the minor in the manner previously mentioned; and that is among things that need no explanation. And because the desired thing in this context is that the major be a definition of the minor; and that does not follow from the syllogism. As for that its acquisition cannot be by division, because division entails indefinite divisions, for positing one of the divisions determinately to be a definition would be a positing that is beneficial, not derived from division. And if one excludes the contradictory of some divisions to produce the remainder, as it is said: The definition of man is either rational animal or non-rational animal; the second is not a definition, so the definition is the first. Or it is said: Man is either animal or non-animal, but he is not non-animal, therefore he is animal; and by this way it is established that he is rational or mortal. Then all these predicates equivalent to him are collected, and it is also said: They are a detailed statement indicating the quiddity of man. And every detailed statement indicating the quiddity of a thing is its definition. Then it is said: It is not conceded that the division is restricted to the divisions you mentioned; nor is it conceded that the conditional premise is true; it is necessary to adduce a proof for each of them. And on the supposition of conceding, division alone is not beneficial for the definition. And because it is an exposition of a thing by what is more hidden than it, for the definition of a thing and its parts are more manifest relative to it than others. And because the detailed statement mentioned is the definition of definition, so its mediation in the syllogism is a petition of the first desired; for whoever believes that the definition is known only by demonstration does not concede that that statement is a definition, otherwise he does not concede that these predicates equivalent to man are a detailed statement indicating his quiddity. For if that were known, it would be known that they are a definition for him without this mediation, for the meaning of a thing is not manifest to a thing unless it is manifest to it; since it is nothing other than its meaning. So know that the mediation of the definition of the major because it is more manifest for the minor, or the definition of the minor because the major is more manifest for it, does not yield the desired. As for that its acquisition cannot be by induction, because if the definition is predicated of the particulars after inducting them as a definition of each of them insofar as it is determinate, it is false because we have shown that individuals insofar as they are individuals have no definitions because they are among corruptibles. And if we concede that, still the definition of individuals falling under a species is not a definition of the species; for each individual has what the species does not have. And if it is predicated of them as a definition of their species, it is a petition of the desired. And if it is predicated absolutely, it does not necessarily follow that it is a definition of it, even if its predication of it follows, because of the possibility that its predication of it is by another way other than the predication of the definition of the defined. And just as its acquisition cannot be by what has passed, so too it cannot be from the definition of the opposite, as that its definition is the opposite of its opposite; for the definition of the opposite is not free from being acquired from its opposite, in which case circularity follows, or from other than its opposite; and that is subject to denial unless that other is the definition of this thing. Moreover, the definition of one opposite is not more known than the definition of the other opposite; so how can it be acquired? And because it is not necessary that every defined has an opposite. There has already passed what is not receptive of an opposite, like evenness and oddness, straightness and curvature, and others. And even if it were so, it would not be possible from the definition of the opposite. For if it were possible, either it would be in need of it in general; in which case it would follow that what is undefined is defined; or it would not be in need of it at all, in which case it would follow that it is not in need of it when it cannot be from other than it, and that is impossible. Rather, the way in acquiring the defined and its divisions is composition. That is by taking a number of individuals that are not divisible from the totality of the defined, whether the defined is a genus or a species; and seeking all their predicates up to the universal term above which there is no more universal. And those predicates may be essential, and may be accidental: so the essential are distinguished from the accidental by the rules that have been mentioned. Then the most universal essential that has nothing more universal above it is found. Then what is below it among the essentials likewise in order until it ends.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of four alleged methods for acquiring definitions (ḥadd), followed by the proposal of the correct method, which is composition (tarkīb). The author first argues against acquiring definition through syllogism. The syllogism fails because the major term would need to be a definition of the minor, but the syllogism only predicates the major of the minor without guaranteeing that predication is definitional. Moreover, the middle term applies to the minor's differentiae and properties, making the major not a definition of them. The second refutation targets division (qisma). Division yields indefinite branches; to obtain a definition, one must arbitrarily select a branch, which is not derived from division itself. Even if one uses exclusive division (e.g., man is either rational or non-rational animal), this presumes the truth of the conditional premise and the exhaustive nature of the division, both of which require proof. Thus division alone does not produce the definition. The third refutation concerns induction (istiqrā'). Induction cannot yield a definition because individuals as such have no definitions (they are corruptible). Even if we concede definitions for individuals, the definition of individuals does not extend to the species (each individual has unique accidents). Predicating a definition across individuals absolutely does not guarantee it is a definition of the species. The fourth refutation addresses acquiring definition from the opposite (ḍidd). This leads to circularity (if the definition of one opposite depends on the other) or requires an external definition, which is essentially conceding the point. Moreover, not all things have opposites (e.g., evenness, straightness). Thus these four methods are invalid. The correct method is composition (tarkīb): one takes several indivisible individuals of the genus or species, collects all their predicates up to the most universal, separates essential (dhātiyyāt) from accidental (ʿaraḍiyyāt) using established rules, and then arranges the essential predicates from the most universal downward until the definition is reached. The text cuts off mid-explanation.

Defining via Opposite Fails
Refutation of opposite method for definition acquisition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the method of defining a thing via its opposite (ḍidd) leads to circularity and is not always possible.

Core Idea
Defining by opposite either loops back on itself or assumes what it needs to prove.

Some suggested that you can define something by its opposite—e.g., the definition of 'good' is 'what is not evil'. The author refutes this: either the definition of the opposite itself depends on the first (circularity), or it relies on a third term that is actually the definition of the thing. Moreover, not every term has an opposite, so the method is not universal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the proposed method
The method claims that the definition of a thing is the opposite of its opposite's definition. E.g., if you define 'evil', then 'good' is the opposite of that definition.
2
First objection: circularity
To define X by its opposite Y, you need the definition of Y. But if Y is also defined by X, that creates a circle. If Y's definition comes from something else, that something else might actually be the definition of X, making the oppositional method redundant.
3
Second objection: not everything has an opposite
Some things like evenness (zawjiyya) and oddness (fardiyya), straightness and curvature, etc., are pairs, but many concepts lack opposites. For those without opposites, the method is inapplicable.
4
Third objection: epistemological priority
The definition of one opposite is not more known than the other. So there is no epistemic gain.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الدور، أو من غير ضده؛ وذلك في حيز المنع إلا وأن يكون ذلك الغير هو حد هذا الشيء . ثم حد أحد الضدين ليس أعرف من حد الضد الآخر؛ فكيف يمكن اكتسابه ولأنه لا يلزم أن يكون لكل محددة ضد. وقد مر من قبل ما لا يكون قابلا للضد به كالزوجية والفردية والاستقامة والانحناء وغير ذلك. ولو كان كذلك فلا يمكن من حد الضد. فإنه إذا أمكن فإما أن يفتقر إليه في الجملة؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون محدود ما ليس بمحدود، أو لا يفتقر إليه أصلا وحينئذ يلزم أن لا يكون مفتقرًا إليه إذا لم يمكن من غيره، وإنه محال بل الطريق في اكتساب المحدود وأقسامها هو التركيب. وذلك بأن يؤخذ عدة من الأشخاص التي لا تنقسم من جملة المحدود جنسا كان المحدود أو نوعا؛ ويطلب جميع محمولاتها إلى الأمر العام الذي لا أعم فوقه. وتلك المحمولات قد تكون من الذاتيات، وقد تكون من العرضيات: فتقرر الذاتيات من العرضيات بالقوانين التي مر ذكرها . ثم يوجد الذاتي الأعم الذي لا أعم فوقه. ثم الذي دونه من الذاتيات كذلك على الترتيب إلى أن ينتهي
with the quiddity. And because the major premise is then false, for the middle term as it is obtained for the minor is also obtained for its differentiae and properties; and it is impossible for the major to be a definition of any of them. As for the third, because the syllogism then only yields the predication of the major of the minor in the manner previously mentioned; and that is among things that need no explanation. And because the desired thing in this context is that the major be a definition of the minor; and that does not follow from the syllogism. As for that its acquisition cannot be by division, because division entails indefinite divisions, for positing one of the divisions determinately to be a definition would be a positing that is beneficial, not derived from division. And if one excludes the contradictory of some divisions to produce the remainder, as it is said: The definition of man is either rational animal or non-rational animal; the second is not a definition, so the definition is the first. Or it is said: Man is either animal or non-animal, but he is not non-animal, therefore he is animal; and by this way it is established that he is rational or mortal. Then all these predicates equivalent to him are collected, and it is also said: They are a detailed statement indicating the quiddity of man. And every detailed statement indicating the quiddity of a thing is its definition. Then it is said: It is not conceded that the division is restricted to the divisions you mentioned; nor is it conceded that the conditional premise is true; it is necessary to adduce a proof for each of them. And on the supposition of conceding, division alone is not beneficial for the definition. And because it is an exposition of a thing by what is more hidden than it, for the definition of a thing and its parts are more manifest relative to it than others. And because the detailed statement mentioned is the definition of definition, so its mediation in the syllogism is a petition of the first desired; for whoever believes that the definition is known only by demonstration does not concede that that statement is a definition, otherwise he does not concede that these predicates equivalent to man are a detailed statement indicating his quiddity. For if that were known, it would be known that they are a definition for him without this mediation, for the meaning of a thing is not manifest to a thing unless it is manifest to it; since it is nothing other than its meaning. So know that the mediation of the definition of the major because it is more manifest for the minor, or the definition of the minor because the major is more manifest for it, does not yield the desired. As for that its acquisition cannot be by induction, because if the definition is predicated of the particulars after inducting them as a definition of each of them insofar as it is determinate, it is false because we have shown that individuals insofar as they are individuals have no definitions because they are among corruptibles. And if we concede that, still the definition of individuals falling under a species is not a definition of the species; for each individual has what the species does not have. And if it is predicated of them as a definition of their species, it is a petition of the desired. And if it is predicated absolutely, it does not necessarily follow that it is a definition of it, even if its predication of it follows, because of the possibility that its predication of it is by another way other than the predication of the definition of the defined. And just as its acquisition cannot be by what has passed, so too it cannot be from the definition of the opposite, as that its definition is the opposite of its opposite; for the definition of the opposite is not free from being acquired from its opposite, in which case circularity follows, or from other than its opposite; and that is subject to denial unless that other is the definition of this thing. Moreover, the definition of one opposite is not more known than the definition of the other opposite; so how can it be acquired? And because it is not necessary that every defined has an opposite. There has already passed what is not receptive of an opposite, like evenness and oddness, straightness and curvature, and others. And even if it were so, it would not be possible from the definition of the opposite. For if it were possible, either it would be in need of it in general; in which case it would follow that what is undefined is defined; or it would not be in need of it at all, in which case it would follow that it is not in need of it when it cannot be from other than it, and that is impossible. Rather, the way in acquiring the defined and its divisions is composition. That is by taking a number of individuals that are not divisible from the totality of the defined, whether the defined is a genus or a species; and seeking all their predicates up to the universal term above which there is no more universal. And those predicates may be essential, and may be accidental: so the essential are distinguished from the accidental by the rules that have been mentioned. Then the most universal essential that has nothing more universal above it is found. Then what is below it among the essentials likewise in order until it ends.
Source pages p. 480

Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of four alleged methods for acquiring definitions (ḥadd), followed by the proposal of the correct method, which is composition (tarkīb). The author first argues against acquiring definition through syllogism. The syllogism fails because the major term would need to be a definition of the minor, but the syllogism only predicates the major of the minor without guaranteeing that predication is definitional. Moreover, the middle term applies to the minor's differentiae and properties, making the major not a definition of them. The second refutation targets division (qisma). Division yields indefinite branches; to obtain a definition, one must arbitrarily select a branch, which is not derived from division itself. Even if one uses exclusive division (e.g., man is either rational or non-rational animal), this presumes the truth of the conditional premise and the exhaustive nature of the division, both of which require proof. Thus division alone does not produce the definition. The third refutation concerns induction (istiqrā'). Induction cannot yield a definition because individuals as such have no definitions (they are corruptible). Even if we concede definitions for individuals, the definition of individuals does not extend to the species (each individual has unique accidents). Predicating a definition across individuals absolutely does not guarantee it is a definition of the species. The fourth refutation addresses acquiring definition from the opposite (ḍidd). This leads to circularity (if the definition of one opposite depends on the other) or requires an external definition, which is essentially conceding the point. Moreover, not all things have opposites (e.g., evenness, straightness). Thus these four methods are invalid. The correct method is composition (tarkīb): one takes several indivisible individuals of the genus or species, collects all their predicates up to the most universal, separates essential (dhātiyyāt) from accidental (ʿaraḍiyyāt) using established rules, and then arranges the essential predicates from the most universal downward until the definition is reached. The text cuts off mid-explanation.

Checkpoint
What is one of the author's objections to defining a thing by its opposite?
A) The definition of the opposite is always clearer, making the method easy.
B) It leads to circularity, and not every term has an opposite.
C) It requires induction, which is also invalid.
D) It relies on division, which is already refuted.

Key Takeaway
Defining by opposite is either circular or inapplicable; a true definition must be positive and direct.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Evaluate the definition: 'The permissible (ḥalāl) is what is not forbidden (ḥarām).' Using the author's objections, explain why this is not a real definition.
?
Identify a pair of terms in Islamic law that truly have opposites and explain how defining one by the other would be circular.

intermediate

The Correct Method: Composition (Tarkīb)
Introduction of composition as the correct method for definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the steps of composition (tarkīb) for acquiring a definition, as presented in the passage.

Core Idea
Composition builds definitions from the ground up: collect predicates of individuals, separate essential from accidental, then arrange from most universal downward.

Having refuted four incorrect methods, the author proposes the correct way: composition (tarkīb). This method takes several indivisible individuals (of a genus or species), collects all their predicates up to the most universal term, identifies which predicates are essential (dhātiyyāt) using established rules, and then orders them from the most universal essential down to the specific differentia. This yields a definition that captures the essence.

Guided Path
1
Select indivisible individuals
Choose a number of individuals (juzʾiyyāt) that are not divisible further from the totality of the defined (the genus or species you want to define). These serve as the starting point for data collection.
2
Collect all predicates up to the broadest universal
For each individual, list every predicate applicable to it, going up to the most general category (e.g., 'substance' for material things). This includes both essential and accidental predicates.
3
Separate essential predicates from accidental
Using the rules mentioned earlier (al-qawānīn allatī marra dhikruhā), distinguish which predicates are essential (dhātiyyāt) and which are accidental (ʿaraḍiyyāt). Essential predicates are those that enter into the definition.
4
Arrange essential predicates by universality
From the essential predicates, find the most universal (e.g., genus), then the next less universal (e.g., differentia), and so on, until the definition is complete. This ordered list forms the definition.

بالماهية. ولأن الكبرى كاذبة حينئذ فإن الأوسط كما حصل للأصغر حصل أيضًا لفصوله وخواصه؛ ولا يمكن أن يكون الأكبر حدا لشيء منها. وأما الثالث فلأن القياس حينئذ لا ينتج إلا حمل الأكبر على الأصغر بالوجه الذي مر ذكره؛ وإنه من جملة ما لا حاجة له إلى البيان. ولأن المطلوب في هذا المقام هو أن يكون الأكبر حدا للأصغر؛ وذلك لا يلزم من القياس. وأما أنه لا يمكن أن يكون اكتسابه بالقسمة فلأن القسمة مستلزمة لأقسام غير معينة، فإن وضع قسم منها على التعيين ليكون حدا كان ذلك وضعا مفيدًا لا مستفادًا من القسمة. وإن استثني نقيض بعض الأقسام لإنتاج الباقي كما يقال حد الإنسان إما حيوان ناطق وإما حيوان غير ناطق ؛ والثاني ليس بحد فالحد هو الأول. أو يقال الإنسان إما حيوان وإما غير حيوان لكنه لا يكون غير حيوان فهو إذن حيوان؛ وبهذا الطريق يثبت أنه ناطق أو مائت. ثم يجمع جميع هذه المحمولات المساوية له ويقال أيضًا إنها قول مفصل دال على ماهية الإنسان. وكل قول مفصل دال على ماهية الشيء فهو حده فيقال لا يسلم أن القسمة منحصرة فيما ذكرتم من الأقسام؛ ولا يسلم أن المقدمة الاستثنائية صادقة لا بد من إقامة الدليل على كل واحد منهما. وبتقدير التسليم لا تكون القسمة وحدها مفيدة للحد. ولأنه بيان للشيء بما هو أخفى منه فإن حد الشيء وأجزاؤه أبين بالنسبة إليه من الغير. ولأن القول المفصل الذي مر ذكره حد الحد فتوسطه في القياس يكون مصادرة Commentary
This passage is a critical refutation of four alleged methods for acquiring definitions (ḥadd), followed by the proposal of the correct method, which is composition (tarkīb). The author first argues against acquiring definition through syllogism. The syllogism fails because the major term would need to be a definition of the minor, but the syllogism only predicates the major of the minor without guaranteeing that predication is definitional. Moreover, the middle term applies to the minor's differentiae and properties, making the major not a definition of them. The second refutation targets division (qisma). Division yields indefinite branches; to obtain a definition, one must arbitrarily select a branch, which is not derived from division itself. Even if one uses exclusive division (e.g., man is either rational or non-rational animal), this presumes the truth of the conditional premise and the exhaustive nature of the division, both of which require proof. Thus division alone does not produce the definition. The third refutation concerns induction (istiqrā'). Induction cannot yield a definition because individuals as such have no definitions (they are corruptible). Even if we concede definitions for individuals, the definition of individuals does not extend to the species (each individual has unique accidents). Predicating a definition across individuals absolutely does not guarantee it is a definition of the species. The fourth refutation addresses acquiring definition from the opposite (ḍidd). This leads to circularity (if the definition of one opposite depends on the other) or requires an external definition, which is essentially conceding the point. Moreover, not all things have opposites (e.g., evenness, straightness). Thus these four methods are invalid. The correct method is composition (tarkīb): one takes several indivisible individuals of the genus or species, collects all their predicates up to the most universal, separates essential (dhātiyyāt) from accidental (ʿaraḍiyyāt) using established rules, and then arranges the essential predicates from the most universal downward until the definition is reached. The text cuts off mid-explanation.

Constructing Definitions Through Ordered Composition
Author refutes induction and opposite for definition, establishes composition via division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a definition for any Islamic legal term by ordering essential attributes from most universal to most specific and adding the proximate differentia.

Core Idea
Definitions are built by composition of essential attributes, not by induction or opposites.

The passage argues that definitions cannot be obtained by induction (enumerating particulars) or by reversing the definition of an opposite. These methods lead to circularity or failure to capture essence. Instead, the correct method is composition (tarkib): identify the essential attributes of the definiendum, order them from the most universal to the most specific, and combine them with the proximate differentia. Division (qisma) aids this process by revealing the hierarchical structure of genera and species.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum (mahdud)
Determine the thing you want to define, whether a genus or a species. For example, 'man' (insan) or 'substance' (jawhar).
2
Collect individuals and list their predicates
Take several individuals that fall under the definiendum and list all their predicates (attributes) up to the highest universal.
These predicates include both essential (dhatiyya) and accidental ('aradiyya) attributes.
3
Separate essential from accidental attributes
Use the previously mentioned laws to distinguish essential attributes (those that constitute the essence) from accidental ones. Only essential attributes belong in the definition.
Example: for 'man', essential attributes include 'animal' and 'rational'; accidental includes 'standing'.
4
Order essential attributes from most universal to most specific
Arrange the essential attributes hierarchically: start with the most universal (e.g., 'substance') and proceed downward to the most specific (e.g., 'rational'). This order must not be reversed.
The proximate genus (al-jins al-qarib) may have a special name; if so, use it to imply intermediate genera.
5
Add the proximate differentia (al-fasl al-qarib)
After ordering the universal genera, attach the most specific essential attribute (the differentia) to complete the definition.
Reversing the order, e.g., 'rational animal' (differentia before genus), yields only an incomplete definition.

وأما أنه لا يمكن أن يكون اكتسابه بالاستقراء فلأن الحد إذا حمل على الجزئيات بعد استقرائها على أنه حد لكل منها من حيث هو معين فباطل لما بينا أن الأشخاص من حيث هي أشخاص لا حدود لها لكونها من الفاسدات وإن سلمنا ذلك لكن حد الأشخاص الواقعة تحت النوع لا يكون حدا للنوع؛ فإن لكل واحد من الأشخاص ما ليس للنوع. وإذا حمل عليها على أنه حد نوعها فهو مصادرة على المطلوب. وإذا حمل عليها مطلقا فلا يلزم منه أن يكون حدا له وإن لزم منه حمله عليه لاحتمال أن يكون حمله عليه بطريق آخر غير حمل الحد على المحدود. وكما أنه لا يمكن اكتسابه بما مر فكذلك لا يمكن من حد الضد كما أن حده ضد ضد ضده؛ فإن حد الضد لا يخلو من أن يكتسب من ضده وحينئذ يلزم الدور، أو من غير ضده؛ وذلك في حيز المنع إلا وأن يكون ذلك الغير هو حد هذا الشيء. ثم حد أحد الضدين ليس أعرف من حد الضد الآخر؛ فكيف يمكن اكتسابه ولأنه لا يلزم أن يكون لكل محدودة ضد. وقد مر من قبل ما لا يكون قابلا للضد به كالزوجية والفردية والاستقامة والانحناء وغير ذلك. ولو كان كذلك فلا يمكن من حد الضد. فإنه إذا أمكن فإما أن يفتقر إليه في الجملة؛ وحينئذ يلزم أن يكون محدود ما ليس بمحدود، أو لا يفتقر إليه أصلا وحينئذ يلزم أن لا يكون مفتقرًا إليه إذا لم يمكن من غيره، وإنه محال بل الطريق في اكتساب المحدود وأقسامها هو التركيب. وذلك بأن يؤخذ عدة من الأشخاص التي لا تنقسم من جملة المحدود جنسا كان المحدود أو نوعا؛ ويطلب جميع محمولاتها إلى الأمر العام الذي لا أعم فوقه.
وتلك المحمولات قد تكون من الذاتيات، وقد تكون من العرضيات: فتقرر الذاتيات من العرضيات بالقوانين التي مر ذكرها. ثم يوجد الذاتي الأعم الذي لا أعم فوقه. ثم الذي دونه من الذاتيات كذلك على الترتيب إلى أن ينتهي إلى مقول لا مقول تحته؛ فالقول المؤلف من جميع تلك الذاتيات الحاصلة من التقسيمات المذكورة هو الحد لذلك الشيء. وقد علمت أنه يجب تقديم الأعم فالأعم، واقترانه بالفصول الخاصة. وكل ما يكون من الذاتيات العامة فإنه يدخل في الجنس القريب لا محالة. فإن للجنس اسم خاص فالأول إيراد ذلك الاسم ليدل على غيره من الذاتيات العامة بالتضمن؛ ثم يفيد ذلك الاسم بالفصل القريب. وإن لم يكن للجنس القريب اسم خاص لا بد من ذكر جميع تلك الذاتيات العامة على الترتيب الواقع، ويفديها بالفصل القريب الذي هو أخص الذاتيات المقومة. وإن كان الترتيب على العكس حتى يقدم الذاتي الأخص على الذاتي الأعم لم يكن المؤلف حدا. وقد مر من قبل أن قولنا ناطق حيوان لا يكون حدا كاملا للإنسان. فأما أنه هل يكون هذا ناقصا فقد قيل إنه حد ناقص. ويجب أن تعلم أن القسمة معونة في التركيب والقسمة؛ إما أن تكون بحسب الأجزاء كما مر أولا من الأخص وهو الإنسان مثلا إلى الأعم الذي لا أعم فوقه وهو الجوهر، وإما أن تكون بحسب الجزئيات كما مر ثانيًا من الأعم وهو الجوهر إلى الأخص وهو الإنسان. وذلك لأن القسمة من جملة ما تحفظ به الوسائط ومراتب الأجناس المتوسطة والفصول الخاصة بها في الانقسام إلى المقول في جواب ما هو، وإلى غير المقول على ما عرف، ثم القسمة كما يظهر منها جميع الذاتيات طولا فكذلك يظهر منها الجميع عرضا. والشيء ينقسم تارة إلى القسمين اللذين يكون أحدهما تحت الآخر نحو الجسم إلى النامي وغير النامي؛ وهذه هي القسمة الطولية، وتارة إلى القسمين اللذين لا يكون أحدهما تحت الآخر نحو الجسم إلى الحيوان والجماد؛ وهذه هي القسمة العرضية، ولنقتصر في اقتناص الحد على هذا القدر فإنه من جملة ما لا حاجة له إلى الإطناب، والله أعلم بالصواب.
As for that its acquisition cannot be through induction: because if the definition is predicated on the particulars after their induction as a definition of each one inasmuch as it is a particular, then it is false because we have shown that individuals as individuals have no definitions since they are among the corruptibles. And if we grant that, but the definition of the individuals falling under the species is not a definition of the species; for each individual has what the species does not. And if it is predicated on them as a definition of their species, then it is a petitio principii. And if it is predicated on them absolutely, it does not necessitate that it be a definition of it even if its predication on it follows, because it is possible that its predication on it is by another way besides the predication of definition on the definiendum. And just as its acquisition is not possible by what has passed, so likewise it is not possible from the definition of the opposite; for the definition of the opposite is nothing but the opposite of the definition of its opposite. For the definition of the opposite cannot but be acquired from its opposite, and then circularity follows, or from other than its opposite; and that is in the realm of denial unless that other is the definition of this thing. Moreover, the definition of one of the two opposites is not more known than the definition of the other opposite; so how can it be acquired? And because it is not necessary that every definiendum have an opposite. There has already passed what is not receptive of opposite, like evenness and oddness, straightness and curvature, and others. And if it were so, then it is not possible from the definition of the opposite. For if it were possible, then either it depends on it in general, and then it would be necessary that what is not defined be defined, or it does not depend on it at all, and then it would be necessary that it not depend on it when it is not possible from other than it, and that is impossible. Rather, the way to acquire the definiendum and its divisions is composition. That is by taking several of the individuals that do not divide from the totality of the definiendum, whether the definiendum is a genus or a species; and seeking all their predications up to the universal term above which there is no more universal. And those predications may be from the essential attributes, and may be from the accidental attributes: so the essential attributes are distinguished from the accidental attributes by the laws that have been mentioned. Then the most universal essential attribute above which there is no more universal is found. Then that below it from the essential attributes likewise in order until it ends at a predicative term under which there is no predicative term; so the expression composed of all those essential attributes obtained from the mentioned divisions is the definition of that thing. And you have known that the more universal must be presented first, and it is conjoined with the specific differentiae. And whatever is from the universal essential attributes inevitably enters into the proximate genus. For the proximate genus has an especial name, so first that name is introduced to indicate other than it from the universal essential attributes by implication; then that name is informed by the proximate differentia. And if the proximate genus does not have an especial name, one must mention all those universal essential attributes in the actual order, and inform them by the proximate differentia which is the most specific of the constitutive essential attributes. And if the order is reversed so that the more specific essential attribute is presented before the more universal essential attribute, then the composition is not a definition. It has previously passed that our saying 'rational animal' is not a complete definition of man. As for whether this is incomplete, it has been said that it is an incomplete definition. And you must know that division aids composition. Division: either according to the parts, as first passed from the more specific, e.g. man, to the more universal above which there is no more universal, i.e. substance; or according to the particulars, as second passed from the more universal, i.e. substance, to the more specific, i.e. man. That is because division is among the things by which the intermediaries and the ranks of intermediate genera and their specific differentiae are preserved in the division into what is predicated in answer to 'what is it?' and what is not predicated as known. Then division, just as all the essential attributes appear from it longitudinally, so also all appear from it laterally. And a thing is sometimes divided into two divisions one of which is under the other, like body into growing and non-growing; and this is longitudinal division; and sometimes into two divisions one of which is not under the other, like body into animal and inanimate; and this is lateral division. And let us suffice in hunting the definition with this amount, for it is among what has no need for prolixity. And God knows best the truth.
Source pages p. 481

Commentary
This passage is a detailed methodological discussion on how definitions are acquired. It begins by refuting two alternative methods: induction and definition via opposites. The author argues that induction fails because individuals as such have no definitions (since they are perishable), and even if we consider individuals under a species, defining them would either fail to capture the species or commit a petitio principii (مصادرة على المطلوب). Moreover, defining through the opposite leads to circularity (دور) or requires prior knowledge of the opposite's definition, which is equally unknowable. The author also notes that not all things have opposites (e.g., evenness/oddness, straightness/curvature). Having dismissed these, the author presents the correct method: composition (تركيب). This involves taking several indivisible individuals of the definiendum (whether genus or species) and listing all their predicates up to the highest universal. These predicates are sorted into essential (ذاتية) and accidental (عرضية) attributes using previously mentioned rules. Then, from the essential attributes, one identifies the most universal (الأعم الذي لا أعم فوقه) and proceeds downward in order until reaching a predicate under which there is no further predicate. The resulting composite statement is the definition. The passage further explains that the order must place the more universal first, and it must be combined with specific differentiae. If the proximate genus has a name, that name is used to imply other universal essential attributes; then the differentia is added. If not, all universal essential attributes are listed explicitly. Reversing the order (more specific before more universal) invalidates the definition. The example 'rational animal' is cited as not a complete definition because it presents the differentia before the genus. The passage concludes with a discussion of division (قسمة), which aids composition. Division can be longitudinal (e.g., man to substance) or lateral (e.g., body to animal and inanimate). Both types help in identifying all essential attributes and ordering them correctly.

Key Takeaway
Definitions must be constructed by composing essential attributes in order from most universal to most specific, ending with the proximate differentia.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the composition method, construct a definition for the term 'salat' (prayer) by identifying its essential attributes (e.g., 'specific actions and words'), ordering them from most universal (e.g., 'worship') to most specific (e.g., 'commenced with takbir and concluded with taslim'), and adding the proximate differentia.

Constructing a Definition through Division
Author explains how a definition is constructed from essential attributes derived from division.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a correct definition (hadd) by ordering essential attributes from the most general to the most specific, conjoining the proximate genus with its specific differentia.

Core Idea
A proper definition requires essential attributes in correct order, with the proximate genus and specific differentia.

This passage teaches you how to build a definition from scratch using logical division. It is not enough to list attributes; they must be ordered from the most general to the most specific, and the proximate genus must be identified. A mistake in order invalidates the definition. Understanding this method is crucial for precise definition in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the essential attributes (dhatiyyat) of the thing
Determine the set of attributes that constitute the essence of the thing being defined. These include the genus (jins) and differentia (fasl).
Essential attributes are those without which the thing would not be what it is.
2
Order the attributes from most general to most specific
Place the genus first (e.g., 'substance' for human), then the differentia (e.g., 'rational'). The proximate genus should directly subsume the species.
If the order is reversed, the composition is not a definition.
3
Check if the proximate genus has a specific name
If yes, use that name to imply the general attributes; then add the differentia. If not, list all general attributes in order before the differentia.
Example: 'animal' is the proximate genus for 'human'; it has a name, so we say 'rational animal'.
4
Verify that the definition includes all essential attributes
Ensure that no essential attribute is omitted and that the differentia is the most specific constitutive attribute.
The passage notes that 'rational animal' is considered a deficient definition for human because it may not capture all essential attributes.
5
Use division (qisma) as a tool for discovery
Division helps reveal intermediate genera and differentiae. Distinguish between longitudinal division (one part under the other) and transversal division (parts not under each other).
Longitudinal: body → growing/non-growing. Transversal: body → animal/mineral.

إلى مقول لا مقول تحته؛ فالقول المؤلف من جميع تلك الذاتيات الحاصلة من التقسيمات المذكورة هو الحد لذلك الشيء. وقد علمت أنه يجب تقديم الأعم فالأعم، واقترانه بالفصول الخاصة. وكل ما يكون من الذاتيات العامة فإنه يدخل في الجنس القريب لا محالة. فإن للجنس اسم خاص فالأول إيراد ذلك الاسم ليدل على غيره من الذاتيات العامة بالتضمن؛ ثم يفيد ذلك الاسم بالفصل القريب. وإن لم يكن للجنس القريب اسم خاص لا بد من ذكر جميع تلك الذاتيات العامة على الترتيب الواقع، ويفديها بالفصل القريب الذي هو أخص الذاتيات المقومة. وإن كان الترتيب على العكس حتى يقدم الذاتي الأخص على الذاتي الأعم لم يكن المؤلف حدا. وقد مر من قبل أن قولنا ناطق حيوان لا يكون حدا كاملا للإنسان. فأما أنه هل يكون هذا ناقصا فقد قيل إنه حد ناقص. ويجب أن تعلم أن القسمة معونة في التركيب والقسمة؛ إما أن تكون بحسب الأجزاء كما مرَّ أولا من الأخص وهو الإنسان مثلا إلى الأعم الذي لا أعم فوقه وهو الجوهر، وإما أن تكون بحسب الجزئيات كما مر ثانيًا من الأعم وهو الجوهر إلى الأخص وهو الإنسان. وذلك لأن القسمة من جملة ما تحفظ به الوسائط ومراتب الأجناس المتوسطة والفصول الخاصة بها في الانقسام إلى المقول في جواب ما هو، وإلى غير المقول على ما عرف، ثمَّ القسمة كما يظهر منها جميع الذاتيات طولا فكذلك يظهر منها الجميع عرضًا. والشيء ينقسم تارة إلى القسمين اللذين يكون أحدهما تحت الآخر نحو الجسم إلى النامي وغير النامي؛ وهذه هي القسمة الطولية، وتارة إلى القسمين اللذين لا يكون أحدهما تحت الآخر نحو الجسم إلى الحيوان والجماد؛ وهذه هي القسمة العرضية، ولنقتصر في اقتناص الحدّ على هذا القدر فإنه من جملة ما لا حاجة له إلى الإطناب، والله أعلم بالصواب.
To a predicate not predicated under it; thus the statement composed of all those essential attributes resulting from the mentioned divisions is the definition of that thing. You have learned that it is necessary to present the more general first, and to conjoin it with the specific differentiae. Whatever is among the general essential attributes, it enters into the proximate genus necessarily. For the genus has a specific name; then you mention that name to indicate its other general essential attributes by implication; then you benefit that name by the proximate differentia. And if the proximate genus does not have a specific name, you must mention all those general essential attributes in the actual order, and then benefit them by the proximate differentia which is the most specific of the constitutive essential attributes. And if the order is reversed, such that the more specific essential attribute is placed before the more general, the composition does not become a definition. It has already passed that our statement 'rational animal' is not a complete definition for 'human'. As for whether it is a deficient definition, it has been said that it is a deficient definition. And you must know that division is an aid in composition; division may be according to parts as previously done from the most specific, e.g., 'human' to the most general which has nothing more general above it, i.e., 'substance', or it may be according to particulars as previously done from the general, i.e., 'substance' to the most specific, i.e., 'human'. That is because division is among the things by which the intermediate terms and the ranks of intermediate genera and their specific differentiae are preserved in the division into what is predicated in answer to 'what is it' and what is not predicated as known. Then division, as it shows all the essential attributes longitudinally, likewise shows them all transversely. A thing is sometimes divided into two sections, one of which is under the other, like 'body' into 'growing' and 'non-growing'—this is longitudinal division; and sometimes into two sections where neither is under the other, like 'body' into 'animal' and 'mineral'—this is transversal division. And we will suffice in capturing definitions with this amount, for it is among those things that do not require amplification. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 482

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of how to construct a proper definition (hadd) using division (qisma). The author first reiterates that a definition is composed of essential attributes (dhatiyyat) derived from divisions. He emphasizes the necessity of ordering from the more general to the more specific and conjoining the genus with its specific differentia (fasl). The proximate genus is crucial: if it has a specific name, that name can be used to imply the general essential attributes; if not, all general attributes must be listed in order. Reversing the order (specific before general) invalidates the definition. The example 'rational animal' (natiq hayawan) is given as an incomplete definition for human; some scholars accept it as a deficient definition. The author then clarifies that division is an aid to composition and distinguishes two types: division by parts (from specific to most general, e.g., human to substance) and division by particulars (from general to specific, e.g., substance to human). Division preserves the intermediate genera and differentiae. Two modes of division are identified: longitudinal (one division under the other, e.g., body into growing and non-growing) and transversal (neither under the other, e.g., body into animal and mineral). The passage concludes by noting that this suffices for capturing definitions, as no further elaboration is needed.

Key Takeaway
A proper definition must present essential attributes in order from most general to most specific, with the proximate genus and specific differentia correctly conjoined.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Then order them from general to specific and check if the differentia is the most specific constitutive attribute.

Real Definition Requires Existence, Demonstration Proves It
Author argues that definition and demonstration serve different logical functions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between real and nominal definition and explain why demonstration cannot provide a real definition.

Core Idea
Real definition captures essence; existence is a necessary predicate, not part of essence.

This passage tackles a foundational issue in Islamic logic: what can definition tell us? The author argues that a real definition (hadd haqiqi) can only be given for things that actually exist. Demonstration (burhan) may prove existence, but it cannot supply the definition of essence. Understanding this distinction prevents confusion between the roles of definition and proof in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the thesis
Find the opening claim: real definition is only for existent things. Non-existent things can only have a nominal definition (sharh al-ism).
This sets the boundary for what definition can accomplish.
2
Distinguish nominal vs real definition
Note the two senses of 'definition' in the debate: explanation of the name (sharh al-ism) versus real definition (hadd haqiqi). The former does not assert existence; the latter does.
A nominal definition clarifies meaning without claiming the thing exists.
3
Examine the claim about syllogism
The author considers whether definition can be proven by syllogism. He splits the interpretation: either it means nominal definition (impossible, as definition does not need proof) or real definition (the definition refers to an existent).
This leads to two subcases.
4
Analyze the two possibilities
Case 1: definition does not refer to existence – then existence must be known first, making the definition initially nominal. Case 2: definition itself indicates existence – this is impossible because existence is not part of the essence.
The key point: existence is an accidental predicate, not genus or differentia.
5
Conclude the relationship
Demonstration proves existence, turning a nominal definition into a real definition accidentally. But definition per se cannot give existence; it only captures essence.
This clarifies the distinct roles of definition and demonstration.

فصل في تأكيد القول في هذه الأبواب وفي مناسبة بعض البراهين مع الحدود وتنبيه بعض البراهين على الحدود
قد مرَّ من قبل أن الحد الحقيقي لا يمكن أن يكون إلا لموجود الذات. وأما معدوم الذات فقد يكون له قول دال على معنى. ومن ظن أن الحد يبين بالقياس فإما أن يعنى به القول الذي بحسب الاسم من حيث هو كذلك، أو يعنى به الحد الحقيقي. والأول محال فإن شرح الاسم ليس يحتاج أن يبرهن أن المبرهن على أنه يعنى بهذا هذا الاسم بمعنى هذا القول والثاني يقتضي يشار فيه إلى موجود فلا يخلو إما أن يكون الحد لا يشير إلى وجود ذلك الشيء البتة؛ وإنما يعلم وجوده من وجه آخر، أو يكون الحد من نفسه يشير إلى وجوده. فإن كان الحد لا يشير إلى وجوده فقد علم وجوده أولا فيلزم أن يعرف حده أولا لا من حيث هو حد حقيقي بل من حيث هو شرح الاسم حتى عرف ما الشيء الذي هو الموجود. وما يعنى باسم الشيء الذي هو موجود فيما لم يفهم معنى اسمه كيف يفهم وجوده فإن كان وجوده بينا بنفسه يكون ضرورة شرح الاسم حدا له بينا بنفسه. وإن لم يكن بينا بنفسه فالبرهان الذي يبين وجوده كما يبين وجوده يجعل شرح اسمه حدا فيكون الذي كان من قبل شرح اسم قد صار الآن حدا لما صح أن الشيء موجود لا من جهة أن ذلك برهان على حده بالذات بل هو برهان عليه وجوده بالذات، وعلى حده بالعرض لا يمنع وقوعه في الحدود، ولا فيه الخلاف وإن كان الحد نفسه يشير إلى الوجود حتى يكون إعطاء الحد لما لا يكون بين الوجود بيان أنه موجود؛ فيكون من حد الشيء. فقد قاس على وجوده معا من حيث قد حد؛ وإنه محال فإن الحد إنما يبنى على أمور داخلة في ماهية المحدود، والموجود ليس منها؛ فإنه ليس جنسًا ولا فصلا بل هو محمول لازم والحد لا يعطيه لأنه يعطي
Chapter on confirming the discourse in these chapters and on the suitability of some demonstrations with definitions, and some demonstrations indicating definitions. It has already passed that the real definition can only be for an existent in essence. As for a non-existent in essence, there may be a statement indicating a meaning. Whoever thinks that definition is proven by syllogism, then either he means by it the statement according to the name as such, or he means the real definition. The first is impossible, because the explanation of the name does not need to be proven that it indicates this name with this meaning. The second necessitates that it indicates an existent, so it must either be that the definition does not refer to the existence of that thing at all, and its existence is known from another aspect, or that the definition itself refers to its existence. If the definition does not refer to its existence, then its existence is known first, so it follows that its definition is known first, not as a real definition but as an explanation of the name, until it is known what thing is existent. And what is meant by the name of a thing that is existent when the meaning of its name is not understood, how can its existence be understood? If its existence is self-evident, then the explanation of its name necessarily becomes a self-evident definition for it. And if it is not self-evident, then the demonstration that proves its existence, as it proves its existence, turns the explanation of its name into a definition. So what was previously an explanation of the name now becomes a definition, because it is established that the thing is existent, not from the aspect that that is a demonstration of its definition essentially, but rather it is a demonstration of its existence essentially, and of its definition accidentally. This does not prevent it from occurring in definitions, nor is there dispute about it. And if the definition itself refers to existence, such that giving the definition for something whose existence is not apparent is a demonstration that it exists, then it would be from the definition of the thing. Thus it has measured existence together with it from the aspect that it defined, and that is impossible. For definition is built upon matters internal to the essence of the defined, and existence is not among them; for it is not a genus nor a differentia, but rather a necessary predicate, and the definition does not give it because it gives...
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is an epistemological analysis of the relationship between definition (hadd), existence (wujud), and demonstration (burhan). The author begins by stating that a real definition (hadd haqiqi) can only be for something that has essential existence (mawjud al-dhat). For non-existent things, only a nominal definition (sharh al-ism) is possible. The central argument addresses the claim that definition can be proven by syllogism (qiyas). The author distinguishes two interpretations: either 'definition' means the nominal explanation of a name, or it means the real definition. The first is impossible because explaining a name does not require proof. The second implies that the definition refers to an existent. Then two subcases are examined: either the definition does not indicate existence (in which case existence must be known first, and the definition is initially a nominal one), or the definition itself indicates existence. The author argues that if existence is self-evident, the nominal definition becomes a self-evident real definition; if not, demonstration proves existence, turning the nominal definition into a real definition accidentally. However, if the definition itself purports to establish existence, that is impossible because definition is based on internal essential attributes (mahiyya), and existence is an external necessary predicate (mahmul lazim), not a genus or differentia. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the point is clear: definition cannot give existence.

Key Takeaway
Real definition captures essence; existence is an accidental predicate proven by demonstration, not by definition.

?

The Distinction Between Real Definition and Proof
Author argues that real definition cannot be proven by syllogism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a real definition (ḥadd ḥaqīqī) and a verbal definition (sharḥ al-ism), and explain why a syllogism cannot establish a real definition.

Core Idea
Real definition gives essence, proof gives existence; syllogism cannot produce a definition.

In this passage, the author tackles a central question in logic: can a syllogism (qiyās) or demonstrative proof (burhān) give us the real definition of a thing? He argues they cannot, because definition captures essence (māhiyya) while proof establishes existence (wujūd). Understanding this distinction is key to using definitions correctly in the Islamic sciences, where precise definitions of legal and theological terms are foundational.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of definitions
The author distinguishes between a real definition (ḥadd ḥaqīqī), which gives the essence of an existent thing, and a verbal definition (sharḥ al-ism), which merely explains the meaning of a name without requiring existence.
A real definition is composed of genus and differentia; a verbal definition is a stipulation.
2
Understand the role of existence
A real definition can only be for an existent essence. The definition itself does not include existence; existence is an accident (lāzim) external to the essence.
The author states: 'existence is neither genus nor differentia'.
3
Analyze why syllogism cannot give a real definition
A syllogism (or proof) establishes existence, not essence. If one tries to prove a definition via syllogism, it either already presupposes the definition (as verbal) or incorrectly includes existence in the definition. The author uses the example of a triangle: the definition is given first, then existence is proven separately.
Thus, 'syllogism does not establish a definition, nor does a definition indicate existence.'
4
Apply to an Islamic science example
Consider the definition of 'ṣalāh' in fiqh: its real definition includes intentional movements and recitations. The proof that ṣalāh is obligatory comes from revelation (Quran and Sunnah), not from the definition itself.
This shows the separation between definitive essence and proof of existence.

فصل في تأكيد القول في هذه الأبواب وفي مناسبة بعض البراهين مع الحدود وتنبيه بعض البراهين على الحدود
قد مرَّ من قبل أن الحد الحقيقي لا يمكن أن يكون إلا لموجود الذات. وأما معدوم الذات فقد يكون له قول دال على معنى. ومن ظن أن الحد يبين بالقياس فإما أن يعنى به القول الذي بحسب الاسم من حيث هو كذلك، أو يعنى به الحد الحقيقي. والأول محال فإن شرح الاسم ليس يحتاج أن يبرهن أن المبرهن على أنه يعنى بهذا هذا الاسم بمعنى هذا القول والثاني يقتضي يشار فيه إلى موجود فلا يخلو إما أن يكون الحد لا يشير إلى وجود ذلك الشيء البتة؛ وإنما يُعلم وجوده من وجه آخر، أو يكون الحد من نفسه يشير إلى وجوده. فإن كان الحد لا يشير إلى وجوده فقد علم وجوده أولا فيلزم أن يعرف حده أولا لا من حيث هو حد حقيقي بل من حيث هو شرح الاسم حتى عرف ما الشيء الذي هو الموجود. وما يعنى باسم الشيء الذي هو موجود فيما لم يفهم معنى اسمه كيف يفهم وجوده فإن كان وجوده بينا بنفسه يكون ضرورة شرح الاسم حدا له بينا بنفسه. وإن لم يكن بينا بنفسه فالبرهان الذي يبين وجوده كما يبين وجوده يجعل شرح اسمه حدا فيكون الذي كان من قبل شرح اسم قد صار الآن حدا لما صح أن الشيء موجود لا من جهة أن ذلك برهان على حده بالذات بل هو برهان عليه وجوده بالذات، وعلى حده بالعرض لا يمنع وقوعه في الحدود، ولا فيه الخلاف وإن كان الحد نفسه يشير إلى الوجود حتى يكون إعطاء الحد لما لا يكون بين الوجود بيان أنه موجود؛ فيكون من حد الشيء. فقد قاس على وجوده معا من حيث قد حد؛ وإنه محال فإن الحد إنما يبنى على أمور داخلة في ماهية المحدود، والموجود ليس منها؛ فإنه ليس جنسًا ولا فصلا بل هو محمول لازم والحد لا يعطيه لأنه يعطي الأجناس والفصول فقط بل البرهان يعطيه. فإن البرهان المعطي للوجود يعطي وجود محمول الوجود مطلقا أو محمول وجود للشيء؛ وهذه كلها هي اللوازم الخارجة عن الماهية، فلا البرهان يطلب ما هو الداخل في الحد، ولا الحد يعطي ما يعطيه البرهان وهو الذي يكون خارجا عن جوهر الشيء.
ولذلك كان أهل العلوم يميزون مأخذ إعطاء للحدود بابا ويفيضون الحدود إفضاء، ويمرون مأخذ البراهين بابا ويؤلفون البراهين تأليفا. وإذا أعطوا حد المثلث في الهندسة لم يقدموا على ذكر وجوده لشيء بل لم يثبتوا أن هذا حد بالحقيقة أو يُفهم للاسم. فلما برهنوا أن المثلث موجود بالشكل الأول من كتابهم في الأسطقسات صار حينئذ ما كان أهم تفهيما عند ابتداء التعليم حدا بالحقيقة؛ فما أظهر بابان أن مأخذ الحد الحقيقي مباين لمأخذ القياس. وكذلك القول المعرف لماهية الاسم الذي ليس بحد وهو أظهر. وذلك لأن معناه أن هذا الاسم أعني به كذا وكذا؛ وهذا لا يمكن أن ينازع فيه كما لا ينازع في الاسم. وأما أن هذا الشيء حده كذا وكذا فإنه يمكن أن ينازع فيه؛ وبينهما فرق، ولو كان كل قول يطابقه اسم مطابقة يكون لها الاسم يدل على تلك الجملة، والقول يدل على تفصيل ما يدل عليه الاسم حدا لكانت المخاطبات حدوداً بل القصيدة الطويلة أي قصيدة كانت حدا لأنه يمكن أن يسمى باسم واحد مفرد كما يسمى البلد والقرية مع كثرة الأجزاء باسم واحد مفرد. فتبين إذن أن القياس لا يثبت حدا، والحد لا يكون قياسًا، ولا دلالتهما على شيء واحد بعينه فإنه لا قياس على ما يدخل في ما هو. والاستقراء أيضًا إنما هو لإثبات هَلِيَّة بسيطة كانت أو مركبة، وحكمه حكم القياس. وقد يتفق لبعض البراهين منفعة في جنس بعض الحدود، وبالعكس كما أنا لا نطلب لم الشيء إلا بعد أن يضع هل الشيء كذلك لا يعرف ما الشيء إلا بعد أن يعرف هل
Chapter on confirming the discourse on these topics and on the suitability of some proofs with definitions and the indication of some proofs to definitions. It has passed before that the real definition can only be for an existent essence. As for a non-existent essence, it may have a statement indicating a meaning. Whoever thinks that the definition is clarified by syllogism—either he means by it the statement according to the name insofar as it is such, or he means by it the real definition. The first is impossible, for the explanation of the name does not need a proof that the one proving means by this name the meaning of this statement. The second requires that it refers to an existent; then it is either that the definition does not at all indicate the existence of that thing, but its existence is known from another aspect, or the definition itself indicates its existence. If the definition does not indicate its existence, then its existence was known first, so it is necessary that its definition is known first not insofar as it is a real definition but insofar as it is an explanation of the name, until it is known what the thing that is existent is. And what is meant by the name of the thing that is existent? How can its existence be understood when the meaning of its name is not understood? If its existence is self-evident, then the explanation of the name necessarily becomes a definition for it that is self-evident. If it is not self-evident, then the proof that clarifies its existence—as it clarifies its existence—makes the explanation of its name a definition. So that which was earlier an explanation of the name now becomes a definition because it is established that the thing exists, not insofar as that is a proof of its definition essentially, but it is a proof of its existence essentially, and of its definition accidentally. This does not prevent it from occurring among definitions, nor is there disagreement about it. If the definition itself indicates existence, so that giving the definition for what is not manifest in existence is a clarification that it exists, then it would be part of definining the thing. Thus he has measured both onto its existence from where he defined; but that is impossible, because definition is built only on matters internal to the quiddity of the defined, and existence is not among them; for it is neither a genus nor a differentia, but an inherent accident. The definition does not give it because it gives only genera and differentiae, but the proof gives it. For the proof that gives existence gives the existence of the predicate 'existence' absolutely or a predicate of existence for the thing; and all these are necessary concomitants external to the quiddity. So neither does the proof seek what is internal to the definition, nor does the definition give what the proof gives, which is external to the essence of the thing. Therefore, the scholars of the sciences distinguish the avenue of giving definitions as one part, and they dispense definitions liberally; and they pass the avenue of proofs as another part, and they compose proofs systematically. When they give the definition of the triangle in geometry, they do not proceed to mention its existence at all; rather, they do not establish that this is a real definition or an understanding of the name. Then when they prove that the triangle exists through the first figure of their book on the Elements, what was most important for understanding at the beginning of instruction becomes a real definition. Thus it becomes clear that the avenue of real definition is distinct from the avenue of syllogism. Similarly, the statement that clarifies the quiddity of the name which is not a definition is more apparent. That is because its meaning is: 'I mean by this name such and such.' This cannot be disputed, just as the name is not disputed. As for 'The definition of this thing is such and such,' it can be disputed; there is a difference between them. If every statement that corresponds to a name—the correspondence being that the name indicates that whole, and the statement indicates the details of what the name indicates—were a definition, then conversations would be definitions; rather, a long poem, any poem, would be a definition, because it can be named by a single name just as a city and a village with many parts are named by a single name. It is thus clear that syllogism does not establish a definition, and a definition is not a syllogism; nor do they indicate one and the same thing, for there is no syllogism about what enters into 'what it is.' Induction also is only for establishing a 'whetherness' (existence), whether simple or composite, and its ruling is the ruling of syllogism. It may happen that some proofs have benefit in the genus of some definitions, and vice versa, just as we do not seek the 'why' of a thing except after establishing the 'whether' of the thing; similarly, one does not know the 'what' of a thing except after knowing the 'whether'.
Source pages p. 483

Commentary
This passage is a detailed argument distinguishing real definitions (ḥadd ḥaqīqī) from verbal definitions (sharḥ al-ism) and from proofs (burhān). The author begins by stating that a real definition can only be for an existent essence; a non-existent may have a descriptive statement but not a real definition. The main contention is against those who think that a definition can be established by syllogism (qiyās). The author splits this into two possibilities: either they mean a verbal definition (explanation of the name) or a real definition. The first is impossible because explaining a name does not require proof; it is a stipulation. The second, a real definition, must refer to an existent. If the definition does not indicate existence, then existence must be known beforehand, which would mean the definition is actually a verbal definition. If the definition itself indicates existence, then giving the definition would include existence, but existence is external to the essence (māhiyya). The author then explains that definition is built on internal matters (genus and differentia), while existence is an accident (lāzim) that is outside the quiddity. Therefore, definition gives only genera and differentiae, while proof gives existence. The author uses the example of the triangle in geometry: initially, the definition is given without proving existence; later, when existence is proved via the first figure, the definition becomes a real definition. This shows that the means of obtaining definitions is separate from that of proofs. The author further illustrates by mentioning that a verbal definition (like 'I mean by this name such and such') cannot be disputed, whereas a real definition can be disputed. He also argues that if every statement clarifying a name were a definition, then any long poem that can be named would be a definition, which is absurd. Conclusively, syllogism cannot establish a definition; they are different in what they indicate. Induction (istiqrā') also serves only to establish existence, not definition. Finally, the author notes a mutual benefit: proofs can help in some definitions and vice versa, but they remain distinct.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Demonstration and Definition Are Distinct
Author proves that demonstration does not give definition and vice versa.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between demonstration (burhan) and definition (hadd) and explain why a syllogism cannot prove an essence.

Core Idea
Demonstration gives existence; definition gives essence; they are separate doors of knowledge.

This passage clarifies a fundamental distinction in Islamic logic: demonstration (burhan) proves that something exists or has certain attributes, while definition (hadd) reveals what something is (its essence). The author warns against confusing these two operations, using geometry and language as examples. Understanding this distinction prevents errors in reasoning across all Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of knowledge
Recognize that the author distinguishes between knowledge of existence (ثبوت الوجود) and knowledge of essence (الماهية). Demonstration deals with the former, definition with the latter.
This is the foundational contrast of the passage.
2
Analyze the geometry example
Notice how a triangle is first defined (three-sided figure) without proving its existence. Later, a demonstration (e.g., Euclid's construction) proves that such a triangle exists. Only then does the definition become 'real' (حد بالحقيقة).
The example shows that definition precedes demonstration in order of teaching.
3
Contrast real definition with verbal explanation
A verbal definition (شرح الاسم) merely clarifies the meaning of a name and is indisputable. A real definition (حد حقيقي) states the essence and can be disputed. The author uses the poem argument to show that if every explanation of a name were a real definition, absurdities would follow.
This reinforces that real definition is about essence, not just naming.
4
Synthesize the conclusion
The author concludes: syllogism does not establish definition, definition is not a syllogism, and they do not indicate the same thing. A syllogism cannot deal with what is inside the essence (ما يدخل في ما هو).
This is the key epistemological boundary.
